            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202409295-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4f054e85-db3c-4fe2-abed-80414e3da7d2/adfm202409295-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/4f054e85-db3c-4fe2-abed-80414e3da7d2/adfm202409295-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4f703bd5-0cd0-451b-813c-d6e2eed20752/adfm202409295-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4f054e85-db3c-4fe2-abed-80414e3da7d2/adfm202409295-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202409295-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202409295" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The analysis of morphology and internal structure: SEM, TEM, HRTEM, and SAED for FP (A1–A3), for FD (B1–B3), for FF (C1–C3), and Mapping images of FF (D1–D5).</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The angle of lattice fringes between Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S (207) and Sb (104) crystal planes was ≈135°, displaying the larger m of 17.9%. Based on previous reports, the improved m values mean increased lattice distortion and crystal defects, facilitating the improvement of conductivity and electrochemical reaction kinetics/reversibility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0008_R_d93046700e1303" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - J. Colloid Interface Sci. ACS Nano Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Energy Mater. Rare Met.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0013_R_d93046700e1303" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Energy Mater.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> From the corresponding SAED patterns (inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0004">4C3</a>), it could be found that two bright diffraction rings corresponded to Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S (207) and Sb (104) plane of FF, matching well with the TEM results above.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0024_R_d93046700e1314" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Electrochim. Acta">24</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0039_R_d93046700e1314" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the elemental mapping images were shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0004">4D1–5</a>, Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6d1–d4,e1–e5</a>, (Supporting Information) further confirming the homogeneous distribution of Fe, Sb, S, and C in FF. Actually, the adequate contact and uniform binding of the M/S element was beneficial for the stable anchoring and controlling of Fe/Sb phases toward the S phase, thus resulting in remarkable reversibility and Na<sup>+</sup> storage ability.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202409295-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4fbbfb4e-c286-4a83-9782-892108636b0e/adfm202409295-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/4fbbfb4e-c286-4a83-9782-892108636b0e/adfm202409295-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/869661ae-3cb4-4c6a-ad69-6c251c03fb5b/adfm202409295-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4fbbfb4e-c286-4a83-9782-892108636b0e/adfm202409295-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202409295-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202409295" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The analysis of electrochemical properties of as-resulted samples: the initial galvanostatic charge-discharge (GCD) profiles at a) 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, b) cycling stability at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the sodiation–desodiation curves from 2nd –100th at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> of d) FD and e) FF, the differential median (<i>dQ/dV</i>) curves from 1st to 100th at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> of g) FD and h) FF, j) cycling stability at 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, k) charging capacity contribution of conversion/alloying reaction, the charge–discharge curves of FF at stepwise current densities c) from 0.1 to 20.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, f) rate properties, i) capacity retention rates compared to the capacity of their 1st cycle, l) comparison of the Ultrahigh rate capability of this work with that of the previously reported anodes in SIB.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Based on the above captivating analysis, the preparation mechanism of FF was proposed in <b>Scheme</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0010">1</a>. Where the synergetic effects of vacuum calcination and gasification were in favor of strengthening the reaction energy between purified natural stibnite (Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>) and ferrocene, inducing the successful preparation of flower-like FF nanosheets with double-layers heterojunctions (Fe/Sb and Sb/C heterojunction). Assisted by high reaction energy during vacuum, gas-phase ferrocene was preferentially pyrolyzed into Fe nanoparticles and active C atoms, which served as iron and carbon sources. Owing to its strong metallicity, Fe would competitively loot S element from gas-phase Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and carry out the primary assembly/interfacial bonding. Then, Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S@Sb nucleus with inner Fe/Sb heterojunction was formed by in situ nucleation, accompanied by the interfacial Fe–S-Sb bonds. Profiting from its catalysis, the carbon matrix was nucleated and grown around Fe1-xS@Sb nucleus, thus conducting the secondary assembly and outer Sb/C heterojunction construction through an effective C–S–Sb “bridge” bond. Finally, to lower the surface energy, they were tightly bunched and self-assembled to flower-like FF with double-layers heterojunctions. As a result, through vacuum gas-phase regeneration and twice in situ assembly, the bimetallic phases/boundary defects, interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe “bridge” bonds and built-in electric field were formed with strong electronic coupling effect and abundant active sites, contributing to alleviate M/S phase separation, Fe/Sb nanoparticles coarsening and soluble NaPSs shuttling, significantly enhancing electrical conductivity and conversion-alloying reaction kinetics/reversibility.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202409295-fig-0010"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/47ea845c-984c-449c-bfa7-a56920a6bd73/adfm202409295-fig-0010-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/47ea845c-984c-449c-bfa7-a56920a6bd73/adfm202409295-fig-0010-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6bdb6301-dc69-441f-9eab-92a69ca692c3/adfm202409295-fig-0010-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/47ea845c-984c-449c-bfa7-a56920a6bd73/adfm202409295-fig-0010-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Scheme 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202409295-fig-0010&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202409295" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The mechanism diagram of flower-like Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S@Sb@C.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202409295-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202409295-sec-0050-title">2.3 Exploring the Electrochemical Properties of As-Obtained Samples</h3>
            
            <p>Attracted by the significant advantage of double-layers heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe bonds, the relevant electrochemical behaviors were explored as shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5</a>. First, the 1st galvanostatic charge-discharge (GCD) profiles of as-obtained samples at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> were exhibited in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5a</a>, their initial charge–discharge capacities were 548.4/1002.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for FP, 679.3/863.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for FD and 547.4/703.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for FF, corresponding to initial coulombic efficiencies (ICEs) of 54.7%, 78.6% and 77.8%, respectively. After 100 cycles, their reversible capacity could be maintained at 41.8, 189.8, and 546.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, and the corresponding capacity retention was ≈4.2%, 22.0%, and 77.6%, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5b</a>). The high ICEs and excellent capacity stabilities of FF were noticed, mainly ascribed to two aspects: 1) the reduction of nanosheet size and graphitic carbon capsulation could effectively alleviate electrolyte decomposition and irreversible interfacial side reactions. 2) Benefitting from the construction of double-layer heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe bonds, the bimetallic phases/boundary defects and built-in electric field were formed with the strong electronic coupling effect and rich active storage sites, promoting fast ion/e<sup>−</sup> diffusion and tight S phase adsorption.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0009_R_d93046700e1437" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Ceram. Int. Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0012_R_d93046700e1437" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Chem. Eng. J. Energy Storage Mater.">12</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0016_R_d93046700e1437" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Nano-Micro Lett. Sci. China: Chem. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Mater. Chem. A Energy Storage Mater. Energy Storage Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> That is M/S phase separation, Fe/Sb nanoparticles agglomeration/coarsening, and soluble NaPSs shuttling could be effectively inhibited, bringing about considerable conversion reaction kinetics and reversibility. In addition, compared to FP and FD, FF displayed the lowered discharge platform, indicating the potential of full battery application with high specific energy.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0040_R_d93046700e1442" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - J. Mater. Chem. A">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To further reveal the electrochemical process of FP, FD, and FF, their galvanostatic charge–discharge profiles and corresponding differential capacity versus potential curves (<i>dQ/dV</i>) at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> from 2nd to 100th cycles were displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5d,e,g,h</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information). The gradual fading of charge–discharge platforms and redox peaks for FP and FD were noted, perhaps derived from the poor reversibility and kinetics of conversion-alloying reaction during cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0002_R_d93046700e1458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Nano Energy Adv. Energy Mater. Nano Res. Adv. Funct. Mater. J. Mater. Chem. A">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In other words, owing to the inadequate M/S phase distribution/contact, the M phase was difficult to control/anchor S phase effectively, thus resulting in the incomplete conversion and serious separation of intermediate products, accompanied by Fe/Sb nanoparticles agglomeration/coarsening and soluble NaPSs shuttling during desodiation process. And that explained their capacity fading. While for FF, the overlapping curves and stable redox peaks (particularly the oxidation peaks located at 0.75-1.00&nbsp;V) were shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5e,h</a>, suggesting the excellent conversion-alloying reaction kinetics/reversibility induced through double-layers heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe bonds. Excitingly, the reversible capacity of FF remained at 489.1/395.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a retention rate of 69.5/56.2% after 150/200 loops (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8a</a>), much better than that of FP and FD, further revealing its superior long-term cycling stability. Meanwhile, the slight capacity attenuation of FF from 100th to 200th cycles was noted, perhaps derived from the consumption/decomposition of electrolytes and the cumulation of volume change/ mechanical stresses during the long-time/repetitive discharging–charging process. In addition, from its GCD profiles and corresponding <i>dQ/dV</i> curves in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8b, c</a>, it could be found that FF still proposes similar sodiation–desodiation platforms and relatively stable redox reaction process for 2nd–200th cycles, mainly attributed to its creative structural designing. That is to say, this unique structural evolution could alleviate M/S phase separation and Fe/Sb nanoparticles coarsening during the sodiation–desodiation process, facilitating the tight coupling/anchoring of M/S phase and complete transformation of intermediate products (Na<sub>3</sub>Sb/Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S), leading to highly reversible conversion-alloying reaction.</p>
            
            <p>As known, the ultra-fast charge–discharge ability was a key parameter in evaluating electrodes for applications in SIBs. Hence, even at large current densities of 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, FF delivered a considerable reversible capacity of 397.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with capacity retention of ≈83.1% after 100 cycles, better than those of FD (48.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 11.0%) and FP (40.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 29.2%), verifying its considerable cycling stability and Na-storage capacity (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5j</a>). To further verify the significance of double-layer heterojunctions for de-conversion/alloying reaction, the capacity contribution of charging from 0.01 to 2.5&nbsp;V at 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> was shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5k</a> (from 5th to 100th). For FP and FD, the obvious decreasing from 60.9/86.2% to 40.7/46.9% at 0.01-2.0&nbsp;V was noted, revealing the unsatisfactory reversibility of conversion/alloying process and sluggish electrochemical kinetics resulted from the serious M/S phase separation, volume pulverization and NaPSs “shuttling effect”. In contrast, the capacity contribution of FF was kept at ≈85.0% without any fading, further confirming the superiority of double-layers heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe bonds, effectively strengthening two-phase controlling and conversion-alloying reaction reversibility. The <i>dQ/dV</i> curves for 1st–100th cycles of FP, FD, and FF at ultra-high rates in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8d–f</a> (Supporting Information) also supported the above analysis well. In addition, the 100th GCD profiles of target samples at 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> were exhibited in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a> (Supporting Information), it is found that voltage gaps (ΔV) were in order of FP &gt; FD &gt; FF, where the smaller ΔV illustrated the lower ohmic/electrochemical polarization and more stable electrochemical kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0041_R_d93046700e1512" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Attracted by the fast reaction kinetics and electrochemical stability of FF, the Na-ion storage abilities at higher current density were further explored in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a> (Supporting Information). Inspiringly, at 10.0 and 20.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the reversible capacity could be remained at 385.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 70 cycles and 216.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles, respectively, declaring its ultra-fast Na-ion storage capability. As expected, benefitting from the construction of double-layers heterojunctions, the high electrical conductivity, effective controlling/anchoring effect, and excellent reaction stability/reversibility could be induced, thus bringing about considerable energy-storage ability.</p>
            
            <p>Moreover, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5f</a> displayed the rate capabilities of as-obtained samples. At various current densities from 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, 10.0 and 20.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity of FF could reach up to 636.1/612.0/577.1/552.8/520.1/464.3/419.4/334.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, much better than those of FD (650.6/594.7/554.1/496.7/451.5/352.9/257.6/155.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and FP (492.1/225.7/147.5/105.2/72.5/47.9/31.7/30.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). According to previous work, with the gradual increasing of current density, more ions/electrons were first deposited on the electrode surface, accompanied by the increasing over-potential, steep lowering of discharged platforms, and uncompleted electrochemical reactions, finally resulting in serious capacity degradation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0004_R_d93046700e1541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Chem. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Mater. Interfaces">4</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0009_R_d93046700e1541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Ceram. Int. Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Considering the physical-chemical advantages, it could be speculated that the excellent rate abilities of FF are mainly derived from the strengthening of the built-in electric field and electronic coupling effect induced by double-layers heterojunctions. That is to say, the construction of interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe “bridge” bonds would accelerate the diffusion of ion/e<sup>−</sup> from the surface to the interior and react with more active sites. FF delivered the average capacity of 635.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, higher than that of FD (518.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and FP (178.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) as the current density returned to 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. In addition, using the capacity at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> as standard, the excellent capacity retention of FF at the stepwise current densities was noted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5i</a>, far better than that of FD and FP. In particular, the capacity retention at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup> was in order of FF (52.5%) &gt; FD (23.8%) &gt; FP (6.1%), further revealing its considerable recovery ability and cycling stability. In addition, as displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5c</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information), FF exhibited the more stable sodiation–desodiation platforms and a smaller over-potential (ΔV) than FD and FP, disclosing its high-reversible phase transformation and electrochemical kinetic behaviors. On the other hand, by comparing the Na-ion storage ability of previously reported anodes as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0005">5l</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information), it could be clearly seen that FF possessed the superior ultra-fast rate capability in this work, further demonstrating the unique advantages of double-layers heterojunctions and C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe “bridge” bonds.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202409295-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202409295-sec-0060-title">2.4 Exploring the Electrochemical Kinetics and Structure Evolution of As-Obtained Samples</h3>
            
            <p>To study the detailed electrochemical reaction mechanism of as-obtained samples, the in-depth kinetic analysis and capacitive behaviors exploration were presented in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6</a>. The cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of their initial three cycles at 0.3 mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> from 0.01 to 3.0&nbsp;V were displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6a</a>. For FF, an obvious reduction peak was observed at 0.21&nbsp;V during the initial cathodic scan, mainly attributed to a multi-step sodiation reaction process (associated with the reaction between the sodium and bimetallic sulfides along with electrolyte decomposition).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0007_R_d93046700e1596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Nano-Micro Lett. Nano Energy Solid State Commun. J. Power Sources ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">7</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0023_R_d93046700e1596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Mater. Chem. A Green Energy Environ. J Energy Chem Phys. Chem. Chem. Phys. Inorg. Chem. Front. J. Mater. Sci.: Mater. Electron.">23</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0024_R_d93046700e1596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Electrochim. Acta">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the subsequent cycles, it could be found that the peak has been evolved into four pairs of peaks at 0.86/0.88, 0.65, 0.50/0.52, 0.25/0.28&nbsp;V, corresponding to the Na<sup>+</sup>-intercalation into Fe<sub>1-x</sub>Sb<sub>y</sub>S crystal to form Na-rich phases Na<sub>z</sub>Fe<sub>1-x</sub>Sb<sub>y</sub>S, the transformation of Na<sub>z</sub>Fe<sub>1-x</sub>Sb<sub>y</sub>S into Na<sub>2</sub>S, metallic Fe and Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> accompanied by the formation of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) film, the conversion of Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> into Na<sub>2</sub>S and metallic Sb, and the generation of Na<sub>3</sub>Sb through alloying reaction between Na<sup>+</sup> and metallic Sb, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0014_R_d93046700e1639" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Small">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0016_R_d93046700e1639" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Nano-Micro Lett. Sci. China: Chem. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Mater. Chem. A Energy Storage Mater. Energy Storage Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0024_R_d93046700e1639" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Electrochim. Acta">24</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0033_R_d93046700e1639" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Nano Res. J. Mater. Res.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As for the desodiation process, two oxidation peaks at 0.92/0.91/0.90&nbsp;V and 1.42/1.40/1.39&nbsp;V were detected in the initial and subsequent anodic scans, probably related to the dealloying of Na<sub>3</sub>Sb into Sb, the reversible conversion reaction to form Na<sub>z</sub>Fe<sub>1-x</sub>Sb<sub>y</sub>S and further deintercalation process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0010_R_d93046700e1653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Energy Lett.">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0015_R_d93046700e1653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - ACS Nano">15</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0025_R_d93046700e1653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Alloys Compd. J. Mater. Chem. A Dalton Trans.">25</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0032_R_d93046700e1653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - ACS Nano">32</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0034_R_d93046700e1653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Chem. Eng. J.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Noted that the redox peaks intensity of FD and FP decreased gradually from 1st to 3rd cycles as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a> (Supporting Information), indicating the structural degradation and poor reversibility. That is to say, M/S phase separation and Fe/Sb nanoparticles coarsening and polysulfide shuttling were hardly prevented, resulting in serious capacity fading. In contrast, benefitting from the effective structural evolution of double-layers heterointerface, the overlapped anodic peaks of FF were observed, implying its stable/reversible phase transformations and sodiation–desodiation process. In addition, the GCD curves of their initial three cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> were used to further explore the mechanism of sodium storage. Three discharge platforms located at 3.00–0.70&nbsp;V, 0.70–0.40&nbsp;V, and 0.40–0.01&nbsp;V were revealed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6d</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information), associated with the insertion reaction, conversion reaction, and alloying reaction, respectively (matching well with the above CV analysis).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0002_R_d93046700e1670" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Nano Energy Adv. Energy Mater. Nano Res. Adv. Funct. Mater. J. Mater. Chem. A">2</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0007_R_d93046700e1670" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Nano-Micro Lett. Nano Energy Solid State Commun. J. Power Sources ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Specially, the capacity gap of FF between the initial and subsequent cycles was ≈131 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, far less than that of FD and FP (193 and 793 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>), further indicating its excellent conversion/alloying-reaction kinetics and reversibility. According to the afore-mentioned results, the related sodium storage mechanism of FF could be described as follows:</p>

                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/8df75fea-1b6c-47f8-9a8d-42fbc4c40c72/adfm202409295-math-0009.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202409295:adfm202409295-math-0009" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202409295-math-0009.png">

                           <mrow>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                              <msub>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">z</mi>
                              </msub>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi>
                              <msub>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mn>1</mn>

                                    <mi mathvariant="normal">x</mi>
                                 </mrow>
                              </msub>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi>
                              <msub>

                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">y</mi>
                              </msub>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi>
                              <mo>→</mo>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi>
                              <msub>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mn>1</mn>
                                    <mo>−</mo>
                                    <mi mathvariant="normal">x</mi>
                                 </mrow>
                              </msub>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi>
                              <msub>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">b</mi>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">y</mi>
                              </msub>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi>
                                 <mo linebreak="badbreak">+</mo>
                                 <mi>zN</mi>
                              </mrow>
                              <msup>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                                 <mo>+</mo>
                              </msup>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mo linebreak="badbreak">+</mo>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">z</mi>
                              </mrow>

                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>
                                 <mo>−</mo>
                              </msup>
                           </mrow>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}_{\mathrm{z}}}{\mathrm{F}}{{{\mathrm{e}}}_{{\mathrm{1 - x}}}}{\mathrm{S}}{{{\mathrm{b}}}_{\mathrm{y}}}{\mathrm{S }} \to {\mathrm{ F}}{{{\mathrm{e}}}_{{\mathrm{1 - x}}}}{\mathrm{S}}{{{\mathrm{b}}}_{\mathrm{y}}}{\mathrm{S + zN}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }{\mathrm{ + z}}{{{\mathrm{e}}}^{\mathrm{ - }}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(9)</span></div>
            </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">Fascinated by the superior cycling stability and reversibility of FF, the phase transformation was explored by long-term CV curves at 2.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6b,e</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> (Supporting Information). Obviously, it could be seen that the response currents of redox peaks for FF are far higher than that of FD and FP, meaning its ultra-fast reaction kinetic behaviors. That is, the bimetallic phases/boundary defects, C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe “bridge” bonds, and built-in electric field were formed with a strong electronic coupling effect, obviously shortening the migration path of Na<sup>+</sup>/e<sup>−</sup> and motivating the excellent diffusion/reaction kinetic behaviors. Meanwhile, this also explains the high capacity of FF. Moreover, the peak intensity of FD and FP gradually weakened from 1<sup>st</sup> to 50th loops, confirming their large polarization and sluggish conversion/alloying reaction kinetics. In contrast, the redox peaks of FF remained relatively stable (especially the reduction peak at 0.70–0.01&nbsp;V and the oxidation peak at ≈1.0&nbsp;V, corresponding to the conversion/alloying reaction and dealloying/deconversion process, respectively), primarily ascribed to the strong adsorption/anchoring ability of bimetallic phases (Fe/Sb) toward sulfur phase. It has been confirmed that double-layers heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe “bridge” bonds could inhibit the separation of M/S phase, Fe/Sb nanoparticles coarsening and soluble NaPSs shuttling, thus significantly enhancing electrochemical reaction kinetics/reversibility, accompanied by considerable ion-storage ability. Furthermore, to better investigate Na-ion migration kinetic and storage mechanism on double-layers heterojunctions, the CV curves of as-obtained samples at stepwise scan rates of 0.3 to 0.9&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> from 0.01 to 3.00&nbsp;V were shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6g</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information), exhibiting similar contours. It could be found that the response currents gradually enlarged as the increasing of scanning rates, mainly resulting from the rapid electron transfer and redox reaction process. In addition, according to previous reports, the contour maps of CV curves at different scan rates were used to study electrochemical reaction stability/reversibility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0042_R_d93046700e2328" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6c,f,i</a>, FF displayed stable half-peak widths (oxidation peak: 0.20&nbsp;V, reduction peak: 1.0&nbsp;V) after multiple cycles, much less than that of FD and FP (0.85/1.80&nbsp;V, 2.50/1.25&nbsp;V), indicating its high-reversible phase transformation and redox reaction (especially oxidation process, corresponding to dealloying and deconversion reaction), which was in perfect agreement with above CV results. Even at an ultra-fast scan rate of 2.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, it remained smaller half-peak widths (0.78&nbsp;V) (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information). That further revealed great advantages of double-layers heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe “bridge” bonds. Moreover, the diffusion coefficients (D<sub>Na+</sub>) were determined through Randles-Sevcik analysis (Equation&nbsp;<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202409295-disp-0010" title="Link to equation">10</a>) and calculated by the fitting slope between the peak current and the root of the scan rate (I<sub>P</sub>/v<sup>1/2</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0002_R_d93046700e2352" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Nano Energy Adv. Energy Mater. Nano Res. Adv. Funct. Mater. J. Mater. Chem. A">2</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0041_R_d93046700e2352" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0043_R_d93046700e2352" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nano Energy">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The well-linear relationships were noted, implying their superior diffusion kinetics. As known, the sluggish Na-ion diffusion would bring about serious M/S phase separation/aggregation and irreversible/uneven phase transition during the sodiation–desodiation process, finally accelerating the degradation of capacity and cycling stability. Therefore, the excellent ions diffusion behaviors were a key parameter in evaluating the anode materials for applications in Na-storage.

                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(14)</span></div>where <i>A</i> and <i>C</i><sub>Na+</sub> represent the active electrode area (1.13 cm<sup>2</sup>) and the concentration of sodium ions, n is the number of reaction electrons.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0001_R_d93046700e2515" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Mater. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. Energy Storage Mater. Energy Storage Mater.">1</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0018_R_d93046700e2515" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - J. Mater. Chem. A ACS Nano Small">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6h</a>, the slope values of Peak1 (oxidation) and Peak2 (reduction) were ≈0.25/−0.24 for FP, 2.53/−1.18 for FD and 5.90/−3.19 for FF, corresponding to their D<sub>Na+</sub> values were in the order of FP (0.1/0.1 × 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>) &lt; FD (2.02/0.44 × 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>) &lt; FF (10.95/3.16 × 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>), respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). FF with the relatively large D<sub>Na+</sub> further demonstrated the rich heterointerface/defects and interfacial “bridge” bonds could strengthen the electronic coupling effect and electrical conductivity, thus leading to the outstanding Na-ion migration kinetics. Moreover, in further exploring the Na-ion storage mechanism of as-prepared samples, their capacitive behaviors were evaluated by Equation&nbsp;<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202409295-disp-0011" title="Link to equation">11-12</a>. Where b-value represented different charge-storage mechanisms as an adjustable parameter: a) the electrochemical rate controlling process, corresponding to the diffusion-controlled behaviors (the intercalation, conversion, alloying, and Faradaic reactions); b) the ion-storage capacity controlling process, associated with surface pseudocapacitive-controlled behaviors (the interfacial charge and electrical double-layer effect).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0007_R_d93046700e2554" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Nano-Micro Lett. Nano Energy Solid State Commun. J. Power Sources ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">7</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0009_R_d93046700e2554" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Ceram. Int. Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the improvement of pseudocapacitive contribution was conducive to motivating the fast reaction kinetics and rate capabilities. According to the previous experience of Dunn's reports, with the b-value approaching 1.0, the electrochemical behaviors were dominated by pseudocapacitive behaviors, while the b-value is close to 0.5, indicating the ion diffusion process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0009_R_d93046700e2559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Ceram. Int. Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0024_R_d93046700e2559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Electrochim. Acta">24</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0044_R_d93046700e2559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Nat. Mater.">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Herein, from the linear fitting slopes of log(i) versus log(v) as exhibited in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6j</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a</a> (Supporting Information), it could be found that the b-value of Peak1/Peak2 were in sequence of FF (0.81/0.90) &gt; FD (0.84/0.58) &gt;FP (0.49/0.47), implying that Na-ion storage process of FF was dominated by pseudocapacitive behaviors, facilitating rapid ion diffusion and charge transport, agreeing well with the above analysis. Clearly, the plentiful active sites/defects exposed by double-layer heterojunctions were beneficial for the participation of more ions with different energy barriers toward surface/near-surface reaction, thereby inducing the enhancement of pseudocapacitive contribution and total sodium storage capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0003_R_d93046700e2571" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Besides, the pseudocapacitive contribution of the whole sodiation–desodiation process at various scan rates could be further quantitatively determined through Equations&nbsp;<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202409295-disp-0013" title="Link to equation">13</a> and&nbsp;<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202409295-disp-0014" title="Link to equation">14</a>. Where k<sub>1</sub>v and k<sub>2</sub>v<sup>1/2</sup> stood for pseudocapacitive-controlled contribution and diffusion-controlled contribution, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0013_R_d93046700e2589" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Energy Mater.">13</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0016_R_d93046700e2589" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Nano-Micro Lett. Sci. China: Chem. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Mater. Chem. A Energy Storage Mater. Energy Storage Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0021_R_d93046700e2589" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Chem. Eng. J. Small">21</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0043_R_d93046700e2589" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nano Energy">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Through the equation transformation and subsequent linear fitting of i/v<sup>1/2</sup> versus v<sup>1/2</sup>, it could be concluded that the pseudocapacitive contribution of FF at 0.3 m V s<sup>−1</sup> was ≈87.54%, much higher than that of FD (73.61%) and FP (22.33%) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6k</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18b,c</a>, Supporting Information), mainly ascribed to the interesting chemical/structural evolution on double-layers heterointerface. Moreover, with the increasing of scan rates from 0.3 to 0.9&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0006">6l</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18d</a> (Supporting Information), the pseudocapacitive contribution of FF gradually improved from 87.54% to 95.48% (better than those of 73.61/89.58% for FD and 22.33/46.00% for FP), further revealing the dominant role of surface-controlled behaviors in the sodium storage process, especially at high current density. Meanwhile, this also explained the superior high-rate properties of FF. That is, with the fast increasing of ion/e<sup>−</sup> migration, more Na-ions would be absorbed on the surface of the lattice structure, participating in surface/near-surface activities rather than diffusing into the internal materials. In general, profiting from the construction of double-layers heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe bonds, accompanied by abundant phase boundaries/defects and strong electronic coupling effect, the controlling/anchoring of M/S phase and the integrity/stability of lattice structure could be enhanced, thus bringing about considerable ion diffusion kinetics and capacitive behaviors.</div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">As an important kinetic parameter, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was employed to reveal the internal resistance, diffusion kinetics behaviors, and double capacitance during cycling as displayed in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0007">7</a>. All the Nyquist plots of as-obtained samples (0th, 5th, 10th, 20th, 30th, and 50th) consisted of high-frequency semicircle and low-frequency oblique line (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information), which were closely related to the charge-transfer resistance of electrode/electrolyte interface (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) and Warburg impedance of Na-ion diffusion process (<i>Z</i><sub>w</sub>), respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0003_R_d93046700e2636" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">3</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0004_R_d93046700e2636" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Chem. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Mater. Interfaces">4</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0045_R_d93046700e2636" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, to further explore the interfacial resistance changes between electrolyte, carbon layer, and basic materials, the relative equivalent circuit diagram and simplified interfacial models were exhibited in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0007">7a</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>. Among them, <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> was associated with the nature resistance of cell (including the bulk resistance in the electrolyte, separator, and electrode), <i>R</i><sub>ct1</sub> was the ions transfer resistance of the carbon shell/electrolyte interface or basic materials (Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S@Sb)/carbon layer (S1, [CPE1, R1]), <i>R</i><sub>ct2</sub> was about the charge transfer resistance of SEI films on the carbon layer interface (S2, [CPE2, R2]), CPE1/2 were the corresponding space charge capacitance of S1/2, and W<sub>1</sub> was indexed to the ions diffusion resistance inside Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S@Sb.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0041_R_d93046700e2667" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0046_R_d93046700e2667" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Nano Energy ACS Nano Nano Energy">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> From the EIS fitting results of FP, FD, and FF as shown in <b>Table</b>&nbsp;<a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#adfm202409295-tbl-0001">1</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), it could be found that the <i>R</i><sub>ct1</sub> value of FD and FF (641.1/497.8 Ω) at the 0th cycle was larger than FP (225.3 Ω) and the corresponding CPE1 and I<sub>F</sub> was smaller (CPE<sub>FD</sub> (1.67 × 10<sup>−6</sup> F) &lt; CPE<sub>FF</sub> (3.69 × 10<sup>−6</sup> F) &lt; CPE<sub>FP</sub> (6.07 × 10<sup>−6</sup> F), I<sub>FD</sub> (0.09 × 10<sup>−1</sup>&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>) &lt; I<sub>FF</sub> (0.12 × 10<sup>−1</sup>&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>) &lt; I<sub>FP</sub> (0.25 × 10<sup>−1</sup>&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>)), implying its weak Na-ion transport at the interface S1, which was mostly ascribed to the inadequate infiltration of electrolyte and incomplete activation of carbon coating.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0009_R_d93046700e2719" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Ceram. Int. Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> After 50 cycles, compared to the 0th cycle, the <i>R</i><sub>ct1</sub> value of FD and FF reduced from 641.1/497.8 to 25.10/25.38 Ω, accompanied by the increasing of CPE1 from 1.67/3.69 × 10<sup>−6</sup> to 11.06/1.23 × 10<sup>−5</sup> F. Meanwhile, I<sub>F</sub> increased from 0.09/0.12 × 10<sup>−1</sup> to 2.26/2.24 × 10<sup>−1</sup>&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>, much better than those of FP (<i>R</i><sub>ct1</sub>: 225.30 to 132.00 Ω, CPE: 6.07 × 10<sup>−6</sup> to 2.07 × 10<sup>−5</sup> F, I<sub>F</sub>: 0.25 × 10<sup>−1</sup> to 0.43 × 10<sup>−1</sup>&nbsp;mA cm<sup>−2</sup>). The higher CPE1 would accelerate ion/e<sup>−</sup> accumulation on the interface S1 and create a local Na<sup>+</sup> concentration gradient, which was beneficial for strengthening the driving force of chemical transport for Na-ions and inducing its deep diffusion toward FF cores.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0046_R_d93046700e2761" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Nano Energy ACS Nano Nano Energy">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, for FD and FF, the interface S2 appeared along with the relatively stable <i>R</i><sub>ct2</sub> and CPE2 value of ≈3.00/6.00 Ω and ≈2.00/8.00 × 10<sup>−6</sup> F from 5th to 50th cycles. This interesting phenomenon was mainly attributed to the complete and dense SEI film generated by the pseudocapacitive behaviors of the sodium-ions insertion/extraction, facilitating the lowering of charge transfer energy barriers and the improvement of interfacial conductivity. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0007">7b</a>, the R<sub>total</sub> of FD and FF (R<sub>total</sub> = <i>R</i><sub>ct1</sub> + <i>R</i><sub>ct2</sub>) reduced and then gradually increased to a stable value (≈30 Ω) during 0th −50th cycles, much smaller than that of FP (130–140 Ω), further revealing the advantage of double-layers heterojunctions and interfacial C–S–Sb/Sb–S–Fe bonds for obtaining superior conversion reactions kinetics (agreeing well with the above results). That could effectively inhibit M/S phase separation/coarsening and shorten ion/e<sup>−</sup> diffusion path, improving electrical conductivity and long-term cycling performance. In addition, the Na-ion diffusion kinetics of FP, FD, and FF at different cycling could be assessed from low-frequency regions according to the following equations:

                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{{D}_{Na + }} = (4/\pi \tau ){{({{m}_B}{{V}_B}/{{M}_B}S)}^2}{{(D\Delta Es/D\Delta E\tau )}^2}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(21)</span></div>where <i>ω, f, R, T, A, n, F</i>, and C are angular frequency, frequency (Hz), gas constant (8.314 J mol<sup>−1</sup> K<sup>−1</sup>), absolute temperature (298 K), electrode area (1.13 cm<sup>2</sup>), electronic transfer numbers, Faraday constant (96 485 C mol<sup>−1</sup>) and Na-ion concentration, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0009_R_d93046700e3055" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Ceram. Int. Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0014_R_d93046700e3055" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Small">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0015_R_d93046700e3055" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - ACS Nano">15</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0047_R_d93046700e3055" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to the liner fitting of Z″ versus ω<sup>−1/2</sup>, their Warburg coefficient (σ) and the corresponding D<sub>Na+</sub> were calculated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0007">7c,f</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22a,b</a> (Supporting Information). the D<sub>Na+</sub> of FD and FF at 5th, 10th, 20th, 30th and 50th cycles were ≈11.86/3.32 × 10<sup>−16</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, 4.74/5.68 × 10<sup>−16</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, 17.78/5.60 × 10<sup>−16</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, 25.24/8.00 × 10<sup>−16</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup> and 18.33/13.24 × 10<sup>−16</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, far larger than that of FP (6.71/5.90/3.88/3.41/3.18 × 10<sup>−16</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>), certifying its better conductivity and ion/e<sup>−</sup> transport kinetics. Notably, the obtained results based on EIS were different from those of CV in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a> (Supporting Information), mainly attributed to the different analytical model, initial, and boundary conditions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0003_R_d93046700e3117" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As known, their D<sub>Na+</sub> should be improved along with electrochemical activation, but that of FP was gradually lowering, perhaps ascribed to M/S phase separation, Sb/Fe nanoparticles coarsening, and soluble NaPSs shuttling during the continuous sodiation–desodiation process. Furthermore, from the relationship between phase angle and frequency at the 50th cycle, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0007">7d</a>, it could be observed that the maximum phase angle was in sequence of FF (−56.3°) &gt; FD (−52.3°) &gt; FP (−43.4°), revealing the superior capacity and capacitive behaviors induced by abundant metallic heterointerface and defects, agreeing well with the previous reports.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0004_R_d93046700e3128" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Chem. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Mater. Interfaces">4</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0041_R_d93046700e3128" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0048_R_d93046700e3128" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Electrochim. Acta ACS Nano">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The decreasing characteristic frequency <i>f</i> at a phase angle of −45° was noted, meaning the increasing capacitive resistance. Based on the equation (τ = 1/<i>f</i>), the corresponding condign time constant τ of FF was calculated at ≈1.42 s, lower than that of FD (2.00 s) and FP (+∞), further verifying its rapid frequency response and ion diffusion rate. In addition, as the vital kinetic parameters, the real capacitance (<i>C′</i>) and imaginary capacitance (C″) were applied to evaluate interfacial capacitive behaviors.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0003_R_d93046700e3140" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">3</a>, <a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0009_R_d93046700e3140" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Ceram. Int. Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As exhibited in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22c</a> (Supporting Information), <i>C′</i> was negatively associated with frequency, mainly related to the nature of the electrode-electrolyte interface. Moreover, with the decreasing frequency, <i>C′</i> of FF rose faster than that of FD and FP, indicating its excellent interfacial ions transfer ability, which was in favor of the rapid ion diffusion and improvement of capacitive contribution. Based on Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202409295-disp-0019" title="Link to equation">19</a>), the maximum <i>C′</i> at 0.1&nbsp;Hz was in the order of <i>C′</i><sub>FF</sub> (5.25 F g<sup>−1</sup>) &gt; <i>C′</i><sub>FD</sub> (3.66 F g<sup>−1</sup>) &gt; <i>C′</i><sub>FP</sub> (1.05 F g<sup>−1</sup>). It could be concluded that the enhanced Na-ion storage capability was mostly attributed to the excellent surface/near-surface capacitive behaviors. Meanwhile, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202409295-fig-0007">7e</a> displayed the function plots of C″ versus <i>f</i> to investigate the relaxation time constant (τ<sub>0</sub>) of as-obtained samples. That is the time required to reach &gt; 50% of the total energy storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202409295-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202409295-bib-0004_R_d93046700e3182" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Chem. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Energy Storage Mater. Adv. Mater. Interfaces">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Obviously, that of FF was 2.15 s, smaller than that of FD (2.61s) and FP (3.16s), accompanied by the higher C″ (C″<sub>FF</sub> (3.51 F g<sup>−1</sup>) &gt; C″<sub>FD</sub> (2.83 F g<sup>−1</sup>) &gt; C″<sub>FP</sub> (1.11 F g<sup>−1</sup>)), revealing its ultra-fast interface reaction kinetic and superior pseudocapacitive contribution.</div>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202409295-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/04fa0d51-d64f-4fac-836b-e522ecd73b62/adfm202409295-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/04fa0d51-d64f-4fac-836b-e522ecd73b62/adfm202409295-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/89b1efb0-4665-489e-8133-c4430bcb0a95/adfm202409295-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/04fa0d51-d64f-4fac-836b-e522ecd73b62/adfm202409295-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
